  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_308af1b5-db35-44e9-8e97-b9cf8f229862'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initializeSiwa();

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1111529303" />
    <a title="Elevetha " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11828657-elevetha"><img alt="Elevetha " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1461899805p2/11828657.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1111529303?book_show_action=true">Nov 20, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elevetha " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elevetha " href="/user/show/11828657-elevetha">Elevetha </a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780553214499" href="/book/show/852679.Jo_s_Boys">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1111529303" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15578739728498352268">The book, ladies and gentlemen: (I very much tried to make everything chronological. Anything that isn't, such as Josie whining about acting or whenever the Professor decides to grace the world with his presence, is completely due to my lack of remembrance and also my utter lack of desire to go back through the entire book, rather than skimming for the important bits, as I am already doing.)<br/><br/><br/>Professor: *chortles*<br/><br/>Plumfield: If everybody could just stop acting in plays here, that'd be great.<br/><br/>Nan: ER</span>
  <span id="freeText15578739728498352268" style="display:none">The book, ladies and gentlemen: (I very much tried to make everything chronological. Anything that isn't, such as Josie whining about acting or whenever the Professor decides to grace the world with his presence, is completely due to my lack of remembrance and also my utter lack of desire to go back through the entire book, rather than skimming for the important bits, as I am already doing.)<br /><br /><br />Professor: *chortles*<br /><br />Plumfield: If everybody could just stop acting in plays here, that'd be great.<br /><br />Nan: ERMAGERSH I WANT TO BE A SINGLE DOCTOR LEAVE ME ALONE TOM<br /><br />Tom: But I love you.<br /><br />Me: Damn, they'd be a cute couple.<br /><br />Mrs. Jo: I shall sit down for a few quiet minutes of writing.<br /><br />Random citizens: LET'S MOB THE AUTHOR, DEMAND AUTOGRAPHS, AND STEAL SMALL TRINKETS. <br /><br />Mrs. Jo: I've had just about enough of this. *pretends to be a maid*<br /><br />Observant fanatic: WHY YOU MUST BE THAT AUTHOR.<br /><br />Mrs. Jo: *objects on principle that she's pretending to be a maid*<br /><br />Observant fanatic: No, you're not. Your picture is right there, on the side table. <br /><br />Mrs. Jo: *sullen glare*<br /><br />Josie: *whines about acting*<br /><br />Mrs. Jo: STOP TRYING TO MAKE "ACTING" HAPPEN, JOSIE. IT'S NOT GOING TO HAPPEN.<br /><br />Dan: *arrives*<br /><br />All the ladies: *swoon*<br /><br />Me: Oh, wow, these next two chapters are boring.<br /><br />Ted: I'll just try and kill this here dog. For fun. Because I suck.<br /><br />Rob: *gets bit defending dog and might get rabies from Don, who probably doesn't have rabies but how are they to know that?*<br /><br />Don: *definitely has rabies*<br /><br />Nan: Why are the women always fixing your messes? Oh, that's right, because we're better than you are. Ugh.<br /><br />Professor: I say, what a jolly good joke.<br /><br />Mrs. Jo: Hahahahahahahaha, why aren't we punishing Ted, dearest?<br /><br />Professor: Because I'm a worthless character. I'm not even sure why I'm in this book or why you're married to me. *chortles*<br /><br />Mrs. Jo: Oh. Right.<br /><br />Josie: *almost drowns but totally succeeds in getting an actress to watch her act at a later date*<br /><br />Josie: Totes worth it. *coughs up water*<br /><br />Josie: *tries to act*<br /><br />Miss Cameron: You're cute <s>but I don't hold out much hope for your acting abilities.</s> <br /><br />Miss Cameron: *glorifies Shakespeare*<br /><br />Me: *le sigh*<br /><br />Tom: Um. I fear I have accidentally gotten myself engaged. <br /><br />Mrs. Jo: WHA-<br /><br />Tom: BUT SHE'S PRETTY, SO IT'S OKAY. I'M OKAY. IT'S FINE.<br /><br />Mrs. Jo: I'm sorry, wha-<br /><br />Tom: No, really. I'm embarrassed, sure, and lamenting that Nan isn't jealous, but I can live with this.<br /><br />Mrs. Jo: But how on earth did you manage to get "accidentally" engaged?<br /><br />Tom: ....<br /><br />Tom: It involved bicycles.<br /><br />Me: Well, there goes that ship.<br /><br />Demi: *gets a job or something but no one really cares*<br /><br />Emil: I'm so THANKFUL that I got shipwrecked with this gorgeous girl who I got to save and spend all this time with because we literally got shipwrecked, and yeah sure, there are other people on this tiny boat but the important bit is that we're totally getting engaged by the end of this book all thanks to this shipwreck. #BESTSHIPWRECKEVER<br /><br />Dan: *kills someone*<br /><br />Professor: *chortles* (Of course, he couldn't have known that Dan killed someone. There was something amusing in the paper.)<br /><br />Dan: *rots in prison*<br /><br />Nat: *does something musically inclined over the New Year or something but no one really cares*<br /><br />Plumfield: SERIOUSLY WHAT'S WITH ALL THE PLAYS?<br /><br />Chapter 16: All I am is flirting. <br /><br />Mrs. Jo: There'll be none of-<br /><br />Chapter 16: FLIRT<br /><br />Mrs. Jo: -that.<br /><br />Chapter 16: YOU CAN'T STOP THE FLIRT.<br /><br />Mrs. Jo: *glares*<br /><br />Chapter 16: *whimpers*<br /><br />Chapter 17: I am a large sewing circle and some education and I am all about the girls yay! *feebly waves flag*<br /><br />Chapter 18: Um, I'm not really sure what "Class Day" is all about, but Emil comes back here, announcing his engagement so that's cool.<br /><br />Emil: #BESTSHIPWRECKEVER<br /><br />Dan: I am home. And also damaged. But maybe a better person? Hard to tell.<br /><br />Dan: Also, I think I am in love with Bess. <br /><br />Me: They would also be a cute couple. Maybe if they got together, this book wouldn't have been the <i>biggest</i> waste of my time. <br /><br />Mrs. Jo: Oh, dear heavens, no. Her mum isn't fond of you.<br /><br />Dan: *spends years loving Bess, his guiding star, until he dies*<br /><br />Louisa's ghost: Haha, did you see what I did there? Any hope you ever had of anyone getting together with whom they should get together DIED along with Dan hahaha.<br /><br />Me: Go away, you're dead.<br /><br />Louisa's ghost: AND SO'S YOUR HOPE. *fades away laughing manically*<br /><br /><br />THE END.<br /><br /><br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_244279339" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/244279339" />
    <a title="Jess ❈Harbinger of Blood-Soaked Rainbows❈" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7125124-jess-harbinger-of-blood-soaked-rainbows"><img alt="Jess ❈Harbinger of Blood-Soaked Rainbows❈" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1440512431p2/7125124.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/244279339?book_show_action=true">Dec 07, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jess ❈Harbinger of Blood-Soaked Rainbows❈" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jess ❈Harbinger of Blood-Soaked Rainbows❈" href="/user/show/7125124-jess-harbinger-of-blood-soaked-rainbows">Jess ❈Harbinger of Blood-Soaked Rainbows❈</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780316031035" href="/book/show/1329946.Jo_s_Boys">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7125124-jess-harbinger-of-blood-soaked-rainbows?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7125124-jess-harbinger-of-blood-soaked-rainbows?shelf=classic">classic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7125124-jess-harbinger-of-blood-soaked-rainbows?shelf=beautifully-written-words">beautifully-written-words</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7125124-jess-harbinger-of-blood-soaked-rainbows?shelf=literary-crushes">literary-crushes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7125124-jess-harbinger-of-blood-soaked-rainbows?shelf=a-z-challenge">a-z-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7125124-jess-harbinger-of-blood-soaked-rainbows?shelf=own-read">own-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7125124-jess-harbinger-of-blood-soaked-rainbows?shelf=classic-american-literature">classic-american-literature</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7125124-jess-harbinger-of-blood-soaked-rainbows?shelf=3-stars">3-stars</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer244279339" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5304265421257424446">My A-Z challenge for the year with the lovely and vivacious <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/17243568-karly-the-vampire-ninja?ref=ru_lihp_lk_us_37_mclk-exp71cell164_exp69cell156-up2093469305' rel='nofollow noopener'>Karly</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/18711982-kristin' rel='nofollow noopener'>Kristin</a><a></a> has officially begun! <br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1421296230i/13355329.gif' width='375' height='250' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><b>A is for Alcott<br/><br/><br/>Let the games begin....</b><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1420475663ra/13230033.gif' width='375' height='275' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I always find that reviewing an Alcott book is a bit difficult. I kind of have a love/hate relationship with her. I read <i>Little Women</i> only a few years ago at the request of my mother who loved it, but didn't like the other two books in the series. And honestly, I agree with her. <i>Little Women</i> though moralistic and preachy, is a very beautiful and tender story a</span>
  <span id="freeText5304265421257424446" style="display:none">My A-Z challenge for the year with the lovely and vivacious <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/17243568-karly-the-vampire-ninja?ref=ru_lihp_lk_us_37_mclk-exp71cell164_exp69cell156-up2093469305" rel="nofollow noopener">Karly</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/18711982-kristin" rel="nofollow noopener">Kristin</a><a></a> has officially begun! <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1421296230i/13355329.gif" width="375" height="250" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>A is for Alcott<br><br><br>Let the games begin....</b><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1420475663ra/13230033.gif" width="375" height="275" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I always find that reviewing an Alcott book is a bit difficult. I kind of have a love/hate relationship with her. I read <i>Little Women</i> only a few years ago at the request of my mother who loved it, but didn't like the other two books in the series. And honestly, I agree with her. <i>Little Women</i> though moralistic and preachy, is a very beautiful and tender story about the lives of four sisters and how those lives grow and change every year, into adulthood, and marriage, and motherhood, but that sisterly bond that they have remains strong and steadfast despite the change and distance time has placed on it. <i>Little Men</i> is basically about the students at the school that Jo and her husband have founded, and though there are some sweet and touching moments in that one, I found the complete and utter lack of an ongoing plot rather boring, and as most of the stories contained in it are about the everyday lives of children, I found the whole thing kind of dull. Now in <i>Jo's Boys</i>, the preaching and moralistic side of Alcott is in full force, but I admit, I enjoyed this one much better than the second installment. I will break it down into Pros and Cons.<br><br><b>PROs:</b><br>I still love Jo. She is such an intelligent and witty character, and Alcott has always written her with a lot of depth. Her relationship with her much older husband, Fritz, is absolutely beautifully portrayed here, and I think their brief tender moments beat out any Nicholas Sparks insta-love romance fest any day. The way she cares for the boys and girls at the college she founded is very sweet, and her relationships with many of them are actually very endearing. She was by a mile, my favorite part of this book.<br><br>Dan. Dan. Dan. Dan. Dan. I absolutely love the character of Dan, who was the iconic "bad boy" of Book 2. We see him as an adult in this one, and I completely fell in love with his rugged outdoorsy good looks, and his boyish charm. He still has the "bad boy" thing going on, but Dan has matured, and has a strong will to do something positive with his life, one that his adoptive mother, Jo, can be proud of him for. I longed to read his chapters, and I only wish he were a bigger presence in this book.<br><br>There is much more of a ongoing plot in this one, unlike <i>Little Men</i>, even though stories of each character make up that plot. I found it much more engaging, and a lot less boring that its predecessor.<br><br>I loved Amy and Laurie's daughter Bess and Meg's daughter Josie, and thought they were amazing counterparts to younger Amy and Jo from book 1. Bess is a wonderful artist and Josie is a very talented actress, and I love that Alcott wrote about two such female characters who pursued and were successful in the arts, particularly during a time when women were not as successful in those endeavors.<br><br><b>Ok, now for the CONS</b><br>I really really really don't like what Alcott did to Meg's character. I admit that Meg was always my least favorite of the Little Women, but she is so god-awful in this one I wanted to punch her in the face. She is so moralistic and preachy, and wants her children to be and do exactly what she wants them to do and not what they want to do. She forbids Daisy to marry Nat even though THEY HAVE LOVED EACH OTHER FOR TEN YEARS, simply because Nat isn't rich enough for Daisy. Last time I checked, didn't Meg marry a poor man when her family didn't want her to? And she keeps insisting on a career for Demi that she wants even though Demi obviously wants other things. But Demi, always the dutiful son, wants to please his mother more than he wants to be happy. Barf. Barf. Barf. I wanted Meg to die.<br><br>Adult Amy is SO. BORING. She makes Lissa from <i>Vampire Academy</i> look like Amy Poehler.<br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Seriously? Why is Dan not good enough for Bess? They OBVIOUSLY loved each other. I could tell during the first 10% that there was a major love interest for these two. And its kind of a beauty and the beast thing which could have been awesome, and beautiful, and pure. But NO! Dan is not good enough for perfect Bess who needs someone with wealth and status and power. I would have loved sweet Bess to tame Wild Dan a bit.....but Dan could have given some zest to her as well, taken her out west to paint beautiful landscapes. And these two could have been really happy together. I saw a whole ending planned out for the two of them. I kept believing it would work. But no, Alcott had to take what was left of my romantic impulses and smash them. BOO HISS! Instead Bess ends up marrying some nameless schmuck and Dan ends up dying alone and unmarried. I almost dropped a star because of this. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>All in all, I would say this is a solid three. Right smack dab in the middle. I think I need to be done with Alcott for awhile. Though I absolutely love her beautiful prose, her annyoing habit of preaching gets on my nerves.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="5304265421257424446" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_8226653" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/8226653" />
    <a title="Rachel Brand" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/572197-rachel-brand"><img alt="Rachel Brand" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1517422811p2/572197.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/8226653?book_show_action=true">Oct 25, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rachel Brand" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rachel Brand" href="/user/show/572197-rachel-brand">Rachel Brand</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780140367140" href="/book/show/1434997.Jo_s_Boys">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/572197-rachel-brand?shelf=classics">classics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/572197-rachel-brand?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/572197-rachel-brand?shelf=2008">2008</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer8226653" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14048657474758668190">Finally! I started reading this as soon as I finished Little Men, but didn't really get into so put it down for a few months. Around page 150 I suddenly got hooked on the stories within the book (because every chapter in an Alcott novel has its own individual plot) and read a few chapters every day until I finished it. It's obvious at the end that it's the last book she'll write about the March family as the last page lists what happens to every character - which is a bit sad, as Alcott's novels</span>
  <span id="freeText14048657474758668190" style="display:none">Finally! I started reading this as soon as I finished Little Men, but didn't really get into so put it down for a few months. Around page 150 I suddenly got hooked on the stories within the book (because every chapter in an Alcott novel has its own individual plot) and read a few chapters every day until I finished it. It's obvious at the end that it's the last book she'll write about the March family as the last page lists what happens to every character - which is a bit sad, as Alcott's novels are always such sweet, simple reads. Luckily I have Eight Cousins and Rose in Bloom on my bookcase to read! I once read the synopsis of one of Alcott's older, less-popular novels on Amazon, and it was described as a collection of "wholesome and moralistic stories" which I think is a perfect description of Jo's Boys. A lot of people these days don't like stories which have meanings and morals, but I do. I guess I'm kind of old fashioned in that way - I would love to live in a family similar to that of Jo March's. 9/10</span>
  <a data-text-id="14048657474758668190" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_3306337015" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3306337015" />
    <a title="Kathleen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/48502194-kathleen"><img alt="Kathleen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1447215825p2/48502194.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3306337015?book_show_action=true">May 06, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kathleen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kathleen" href="/user/show/48502194-kathleen">Kathleen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780448060132" href="/book/show/2842979-jo-s-boys">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48502194-kathleen?shelf=classic">classic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48502194-kathleen?shelf=children">children</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48502194-kathleen?shelf=women-writers">women-writers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48502194-kathleen?shelf=writing">writing</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3306337015" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14222802371488537948">Taking place ten years after <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/78950.Little_Men' title='Little Men by Louisa May Alcott' rel='nofollow noopener'>Little Men</a>, Jo’s Boys shows us the Plumfield clan—led by our aging friends from the original story--growing up. Alcott makes you care deeply about her boys and her girls, giving each dramas of their own. Dan becomes a rough and rugged anti-hero, Nat a tempted world-travelling musician, Nan a single-minded doctor. Josie and Ted are much like their namesakes Jo and Laurie: impulsive and fun and always in need of some moral lesson or other.<br/><br/>It’s a book of racial and clas</span>
  <span id="freeText14222802371488537948" style="display:none">Taking place ten years after <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/78950.Little_Men" title="Little Men by Louisa May Alcott" rel="nofollow noopener">Little Men</a>, Jo’s Boys shows us the Plumfield clan—led by our aging friends from the original story--growing up. Alcott makes you care deeply about her boys and her girls, giving each dramas of their own. Dan becomes a rough and rugged anti-hero, Nat a tempted world-travelling musician, Nan a single-minded doctor. Josie and Ted are much like their namesakes Jo and Laurie: impulsive and fun and always in need of some moral lesson or other.<br /><br />It’s a book of racial and class privilege, but for what it is, it is well done. There are some references to woman’s suffrage, and some pretty good answers to the young girls’ questions. <i>“Grandpa, must women always obey men and say they are the wisest, just because they are the strongest?”</i><br /><br />Alcott has her alter-ego become a famous author of children's books, and gives us a chapter about the downside of literary fame, including being hounded with fan mail requests. <i>“Emerson and Whittier put these things in the wastepaper basket; and though only a literary nursery maid who provides moral pap for the young, I will follow their illustrious example …”</i><br /><br />Their little world felt like a utopia to me when I was a young reader, and it was a joy to revisit it. (My copy has the lovely pictures on this cover.) It has been almost half a century, yet there were passages I remembered so well. These little scenes stayed in my mind for all this time! <br /><br />Demi, on his entrance into book publishing: <i>“I am ready to do anything about books, if it’s only to dust them.”</i> That longing popped in my head often when looking for jobs over the years.<br /><br />Josie, in an effort to help her brother come up with a creative marriage proposal: <i>“I read in one of Miss Edgeworth’s stories about a man who offers three roses to his lady—a bud, a half-blown, and a full-blown rose.”</i> How often I thought of that when I was picking roses, long after I remembered where the reference was from.<br /><br />So this book is a part of me, and I was relieved to still enjoy it after so many years. I may have traded the youthful romantic longings that made it my favorite back then, for an appreciation of what it is to watch young people grow into adults, but it still had the power to touch me. <br /><br />I believe Louisa knew a thing or two about life, and how to shape it into a story that can last a lifetime. It has for me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14222802371488537948" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_5734841" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/5734841" />
    <a title="Zoe" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/166594-zoe"><img alt="Zoe" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1194484745p2/166594.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/5734841?book_show_action=true">Sep 05, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Zoe" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Zoe" href="/user/show/166594-zoe">Zoe</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/166594-zoe?shelf=generalfiction">generalfiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer5734841" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15979921286139751181">A long, sometimes tedious, but almost always charming epilogue to Little Women and Little Men. Alcott wrote it in 1886, eighteen years after Little Women and two years before her death. She must have known, feeling the effects of mercury poisoning from her time as a Civil War nurse, that the lights were really going out, the curtain about to fall.<br/><br/>In this book Alcott continues to find a platform for her ideas, including women's suffrage, co-education, rehabilitation for criminals, and temperance,</span>
  <span id="freeText15979921286139751181" style="display:none">A long, sometimes tedious, but almost always charming epilogue to Little Women and Little Men. Alcott wrote it in 1886, eighteen years after Little Women and two years before her death. She must have known, feeling the effects of mercury poisoning from her time as a Civil War nurse, that the lights were really going out, the curtain about to fall.<br /><br />In this book Alcott continues to find a platform for her ideas, including women's suffrage, co-education, rehabilitation for criminals, and temperance, and makes a mini-Republic out of Plumfield where they can play out. Also interesting were Jo's troubles with being a famous writer, which must have echoed Alcott's. <br /><br />This is the only book in the series that often strays from New England - out west, to London, to a shipwreck at sea - and these parts seemed to be either very sparingly drawn or leaning toward melodramatic. It took some suspension of disbelief to read about Emil's shipwreck and daring heroism, and Dan's rescue of twenty men from a flooded mine.<br /><br />Still, I though Jo's Boys gave an interesting window into Alcott's ideas and the changing world of the late 19th century (the telephone and camera both make apperances). It's hard not to read it as a what could have been, given the differences between the characters and the people on which Alcott based them. By the time she wrote Jo's Boys, two of Alcott's sisters had died, one had lost a husband, and Alcott herself had never gotten married.<br /><br />This was a compelling read for me, though, more for its famliar characters and the world it created for them than for its literary genius, and I felt a little sad at the end knowing the curtain had indeed closed on the March family.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15979921286139751181" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1473574682" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1473574682" />
    <a title="Rikke" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4327582-rikke"><img alt="Rikke" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1594580741p2/4327582.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1473574682?book_show_action=true">Dec 19, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rikke" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rikke" href="/user/show/4327582-rikke">Rikke</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781843915133" href="/book/show/21944696-jo-s-boys">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4327582-rikke?shelf=classics">classics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4327582-rikke?shelf=owned-books">owned-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4327582-rikke?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4327582-rikke?shelf=louisa-may-alcott">louisa-may-alcott</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1473574682" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12798778745912330149">There's a certain sense of emptiness that only booklovers will know. Upon closing a dear book and saying goodbye to its variety of language and characters, it can often feel like some precious part of one's soul is left behind and lost forever. And here I am; with a bittersweet lump in my throat and a melancholic longing for something more.<br/><br/>"Jo's Boys" by Louisa May Alcott is different from the other books in this series. It is far more dramatic - even violent at times - in its plot, and is gener</span>
  <span id="freeText12798778745912330149" style="display:none">There's a certain sense of emptiness that only booklovers will know. Upon closing a dear book and saying goodbye to its variety of language and characters, it can often feel like some precious part of one's soul is left behind and lost forever. And here I am; with a bittersweet lump in my throat and a melancholic longing for something more.<br /><br />"Jo's Boys" by Louisa May Alcott is different from the other books in this series. It is far more dramatic - even violent at times - in its plot, and is generally a far cry from the idyllic ending one would have expected.<br />Most of the time I agreed with Alcott's decisions in her characters' fate, but I will not and cannot accept the broken road Dan had to take. I wanted to see him succeed so badly that his dismissed dreams almost felt like a true tragedy. My heart ached for him.<br /><br />However I loved the story of Nat who got everything he deserved, and dear Nan who turned out to be the perfect feminist that Jo failed to become. Emil's experiences added a tone of adventure to the novel, and Tom's lesson was an underlined deja-vu of Laurie's previous experience.<br />Jo's character was also rather interesting, and I loved how Alcott used her for a higher purpose and through her explained the triumphs and trials of being an admired author. It felt very authentic.<br /><br />I started reading "Little Men" and "Jo's Boys" in order to catch glimpses of Meg, Jo and Amy, but I ended up enjoying the new colorful additions to the little group equally. Alcott managed to introduce the new generation with such heartfelt emotion, that I couldn't help but to give in and adore them just as much as the original characters.<br /><br />"And now, having endeavoured to suit everyone by many weddings, few deaths, and as much prosperity as the eternal fitness of things will permit, let the music stop, the lights die out, and the curtain fall for ever on the March family."</span>
  <a data-text-id="12798778745912330149" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3280645494" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3280645494" />
    <a title="Manybooks" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2970379-manybooks"><img alt="Manybooks" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1459773375p2/2970379.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3280645494?book_show_action=true">May 05, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Manybooks" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Manybooks" href="/user/show/2970379-manybooks">Manybooks</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2970379-manybooks?shelf=bad-attitude">bad-attitude</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2970379-manybooks?shelf=families">families</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2970379-manybooks?shelf=boring">boring</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2970379-manybooks?shelf=childrens-literature">childrens-literature</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2970379-manybooks?shelf=preachy">preachy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2970379-manybooks?shelf=book-reviews">book-reviews</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3280645494" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13925592074547955403">Yes indeed, I do have to admit that while <u>Little Women</u> is both brilliant and will always remain a strong and magical personal reading favourite and that <u>Little Men</u> albeit unfortunately not quite as delightful as <u>Little Women</u> is still engagingly readable and as such also a solidly successful sequel, <u>Jo's Boys</u> (the third and also the final instalment of Louisa May Alcott's <i>Little Women</i> series), while I guess that it does provide a decent enough conclusion in so far that it presents and features ho</span>
  <span id="freeText13925592074547955403" style="display:none">Yes indeed, I do have to admit that while <u>Little Women</u> is both brilliant and will always remain a strong and magical personal reading favourite and that <u>Little Men</u> albeit unfortunately not quite as delightful as <u>Little Women</u> is still engagingly readable and as such also a solidly successful sequel, <u>Jo's Boys</u> (the third and also the final instalment of Louisa May Alcott's <i>Little Women</i> series), while I guess that it does provide a decent enough conclusion in so far that it presents and features how in particular the characters encountered as Plumfield students in <u>Little Men</u> live and thrive (or conversely sometimes fail and do not not succeed) as adults, well, <u>Jo's Boys</u> has for me and in my humble opinion for the most part been a rather massively disappointing and indeed also often quite frustrating and even mildly to majorly annoying reading experience. <br /><br />For although both <u>Little Women</u> and <u>Little Men</u> do exhibit and show moralising messages and preachiness (and with the latter, with <u>Little Men</u> considerably more so than <u>Little Women</u> and with rather less subtlety), both novels do from where I am standing still utterly pale when compared to the almost constant and as such also absolutely overwhelming level and amount of sermons and directly in one's proverbial face both religious and cultural, behaviour-based evangelism that seems to literally inhabit almost every single page of <u>Jo's Boys</u>, with in my opinion Louisa May Alcott often totally eschewing engaging story telling techniques in favour of almost continuously hitting her readers over their collective heads with one moralising and message-heavy speech after another, and yes, often in such rapid succession that one cannot even really recover from being evangelised and preached at before another such volley is launched, before in particular Jo Bhaer starts pontificating once again, leaving me with considering <u>Jo's Boys</u> not as generally a reading pleasure but for the most part just a huge and tediously dragging slog. <br /><br />And indeed, even the few instances where I have found relatable and engaging scenarios in <u>Jo's Boys</u>, such as for example Jo trying to hide from fans of her writing (and who are desperate for autographs) and that Nan is allowed to stay single and to just concentrate on her medical studies, these very few instances of untainted delight, they are both too few and far between and equally do not and cannot provide enough engagement and entertainment to successfully contain and mitigate the moralising, this cannot make the over-use of the latter in <u>Jo's Boys</u> feel in any manner less problematic and annoyingly one-sided.<br /><br />Combined with the fact that I have personally also found Dan's story and how he is (and in my opinion rather callously and unfeelingly) prevented by Jo from openly and publicly declaring his love and devotion to and for Bess extremely off-putting (and not to mention incredibly unjust and inherently nasty to boot, considering that the text really does seem to show Bess and Dan's affection for one another to be totally genuine as well as mutual, that they both truly do love and very much cherish one another), while I do not in fact regret having read <u>Jo's Boys</u>, I will also only ever consider it a two star rating at best, as well as pointing out that from the Louisa May Alcott novels I have read to date, <u>Jo's Boys</u> is most definitely the one I have thus far enjoyed the least, that has for the most part not been a joyful but rather just a frustrating and painful reading sojourn.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13925592074547955403" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1297716819" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1297716819" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer12229102014396877427">I grew to love all the characters in Little Men, so one is bound to love this one just as much. There's plenty of laughter and fun in this book. The end bit has some emotional scenes with wandering Dan and I would have loved to see him happy. Ah, but that is life! A lovely read.</span>

  <span id="freeText9298589525204094508" style="display:none"><i>*opens book*</i> Ah, I can’t wait to re-visit all the characters from <i>Little Men</i>.<br /><br /><i>A few chapters later:</i> It’s kind of boring, but all the boys are still awesome, especially Dan. But at least the Josie-wanting-to-be-an-actress thing is interesting. I wish Alcott would focus more on <s>Dan</s> everyone else, though. And am I the only one who sees definite similarities between Nan and Tom’s relationship and Jo and Laurie’s (from <i>Little Women</i>, that is)?<br /><br /><i>Still Later:</i> Nat’s going to rack and ruin in Germany? Meg won’t let him marry Daisy? Emil’s shipwrecked? AND DAN’S IN JAIL FOR MURDER??? WHY CAN’T THERE BE HAPPINESS ANYMORE?<br /><br /><i>*picks up book after abandoning it for several minutes*</i> Emil’s awesome. Well, at least Nat’s getting his life turned around for the better now. Why’s everyone suddenly getting engaged? Why does Alcott stop the story to talk about women’s suffrage for chapters on end?<br /><br /><i>The Dan-Suffering-In-Prison Chapter:</i> MY POOR BABY. HE ONLY DID IT IN SELF-DEFENSE. DON’T DO ANYTHING STUPID AND GET YOUR SENTENCE LENGTHENED. Now he’s crying…OH, MAN, I JUST WANT TO REACH THROUGH THE BOOK AND HUG HIM. *feeeeeeeeeeeeeels*<br /><br /><i>Rest of the book:</i> Well, everything’s turning out okay. Dan’s back home, everyone’s happily married or engaged. EXCEPT DAN. Who, it seems, will never get a happy ending. WHICH IS NOT FAIR. I’m soooo glad Nat and Daisy are going to live happily ever after, though. They’re both sweet. Now she’s wrapping up the story and-DAN DIED. DAN. DIED. DEFENDING THE INDIANS. NOOOOOOOOO.<br /><br /><i>*spends the rest of the day moping around the house because DAN*</i></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14796318914655846779">I just finished reading the entire series of the March family and their descendants. I homeschool and picked up Little Men for inspiration. I gleaned so many wonderful insights for educating young children, finding our personal missions and following your bliss. In reading the entire series, I get a vision of what I want our lives to look like as I raise my children and the kind of experiences I want them to have. It is easy to involve yourself in the lives of the people in these books because y</span>
  <span id="freeText14796318914655846779" style="display:none">I just finished reading the entire series of the March family and their descendants. I homeschool and picked up Little Men for inspiration. I gleaned so many wonderful insights for educating young children, finding our personal missions and following your bliss. In reading the entire series, I get a vision of what I want our lives to look like as I raise my children and the kind of experiences I want them to have. It is easy to involve yourself in the lives of the people in these books because you know a Meg or a Beth or you are a Jo. There is sweetness, sentiment and TRUTH throughout. It is uplifting and inspiring and you will be a better person for having read it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14796318914655846779" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_341010060" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/341010060" />
    <a title="Liss Carmody" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6394786-liss-carmody"><img alt="Liss Carmody" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1316650361p2/6394786.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/341010060?book_show_action=true">Jun 02, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Liss Carmody" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Liss Carmody" href="/user/show/6394786-liss-carmody">Liss Carmody</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer341010060" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12008329942037936573">In all honesty, this is a dreary book. Imagine the epilogue to the Harry Potter Series, which most people agree is somewhat hamfisted and not up to par, if not blatant fan service. Now imagine if J.K. Rowling had written it into a full eighth book, rather than a single chapter. That is what we have here. As the third (or fourth, depending on how you care to look at it) and final installment in the chronicle of the March sisters and their families, this draws much too heavily on the less-compelli</span>
  <span id="freeText12008329942037936573" style="display:none">In all honesty, this is a dreary book. Imagine the epilogue to the Harry Potter Series, which most people agree is somewhat hamfisted and not up to par, if not blatant fan service. Now imagine if J.K. Rowling had written it into a full eighth book, rather than a single chapter. That is what we have here. As the third (or fourth, depending on how you care to look at it) and final installment in the chronicle of the March sisters and their families, this draws much too heavily on the less-compelling Little Men for its characters and basically occupies itself giving small snippets and synopses of what happens to them when they reach adulthood. Half of the characters from Little Men are dismissed completely with two-line summaries, while the ones that remain are each dutifully given their trial, lesson, and ultimate happy ending. Mostly, the boys are married off to faceless but undoubtedly very sweet girls for whom it's impossible to care much, because they are such hollow caricatures. Two of the girls were so young in the preceding book that they are basically introduced fresh, and the best stories in all honesty have to do with their independent aspirations (theatrical Josie and pragmatic doctor Nan). There is a chapter early on in which Jo Bhaer, having acquired some literary success modeled directly off of Alcott's experience, relates the tribulations of being a famous author in that day and age. Of all the moralizing and sermonizing that happens in this book, that chapter rings the truest with both honest experience and humor. Otherwise, I could have been happy having this book compressed down to a single epilogue, a la Harry Potter.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12008329942037936573" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_801569639" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/801569639" />
    <a title="Amanda " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4929450-amanda"><img alt="Amanda " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596561033p2/4929450.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/801569639?book_show_action=true">Dec 27, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amanda " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amanda " href="/user/show/4929450-amanda">Amanda </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer801569639" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14261231158901290702">I've really changed my opinion about <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/372319.Jo_s_Boys' title='Jo's Boys by Louisa May Alcott' rel='nofollow noopener'>Jo's Boys</a> in my reread of this book. I first read this book when I was 14 or 15 and I recall really liking it. Rereading it as an adult really changed my mind about this book, though. I don't know if it's because I've become completely jaded (I hope not) or just because changes taste as one ages, but things definitely changed the second time around. The excessive preachiness was maybe even more apparent in this story than in <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/78950.Little_Men' title='Little Men by Louisa May Alcott' rel='nofollow noopener'>Little Men</a>. I wonder how much of t</span>
  <span id="freeText14261231158901290702" style="display:none">I've really changed my opinion about <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/372319.Jo_s_Boys" title="Jo's Boys by Louisa May Alcott" rel="nofollow noopener">Jo's Boys</a> in my reread of this book. I first read this book when I was 14 or 15 and I recall really liking it. Rereading it as an adult really changed my mind about this book, though. I don't know if it's because I've become completely jaded (I hope not) or just because changes taste as one ages, but things definitely changed the second time around. The excessive preachiness was maybe even more apparent in this story than in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/78950.Little_Men" title="Little Men by Louisa May Alcott" rel="nofollow noopener">Little Men</a>. I wonder how much of the preachiness was due Alcott's own inclinations and how much was due to the pressure from her publisher.<br /><br />I think certain characters in the book kept me reading (Jo, Dan, Nat). I got about 1/3 to 1/2 of the way through the book before I hit a wall. I just wasn't interested in some of the characters, but the narrative was even more of a sticking point with me. There just wasn't much of a plot. The reader jumped from one vignette to another but the only thing that connected them was that they were all at Plumfield together at one point in time. Maybe this cut the muster in Alcott's time but for today's savvy middle grade readers, I don't think it's up to par. I felt like I was watching the movie <i>An Affair to Remember</i> and all of a sudden it cut to a 15 minute song interlude - BORING.<br /><br />There is much more of a ongoing plot in this one, unlike Little Men, even though stories of each character make up that plot. I found it much more engaging, and a lot less boring that its predecessor.<br /><br />In addition, there were some pieces that seem offensive to today's readers. The comment from one of the female characters of "Our brains may be smaller [than men's]" to calling out single women as spinsters and implying that not wanting to get married and raise a family makes a woman subhuman didn't sit well with me. And funnily enough, they seemed to go against Alcott's own goals, or at least outcome, of her own life.<br /><br />I know most adult readers will disagree with me but I actually preferred <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/78950.Little_Men" title="Little Men by Louisa May Alcott" rel="nofollow noopener">Little Men</a> to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/372319.Jo_s_Boys" title="Jo's Boys by Louisa May Alcott" rel="nofollow noopener">Jo's Boys</a>, at least as a young reader. <br /><br />After reading this as an adult reader, I'd downgrade it from a 4 to a 2.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14261231158901290702" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

It is a little slower-paced than Little Women, which is my hands-down favorite out of the series, but it was a thoroughly enjoyable read. The thing I love most about Louisa May Alcott's March family series (Little Women, Good Wives, Little Men and Jo's Boys) is the way she gently weaves her philosophies about childrearing, feminism, education and living a good life into her stories in such a gentle, non-preachy way. This will</span>
  <span id="freeText11995029885940814973" style="display:none">I am sad to see the curtain close on the tales about the March family! It is a little slower-paced than Little Women, which is my hands-down favorite out of the series, but it was a thoroughly enjoyable read. The thing I love most about Louisa May Alcott's March family series (Little Women, Good Wives, Little Men and Jo's Boys) is the way she gently weaves her philosophies about childrearing, feminism, education and living a good life into her stories in such a gentle, non-preachy way. This will be a great book to read to my kids around age 12 or so, and perhaps again when they are contemplating marriage (because I just love her ideas about growing up and getting married as presented in this book). </span>

<div id="review_76017067" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/76017067" />
    <a title="Melody" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/369112-melody"><img alt="Melody" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1291050708p2/369112.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/76017067?book_show_action=true">Oct 28, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melody" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melody" href="/user/show/369112-melody">Melody</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/6669868-jo-s-boys">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer76017067" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11054976143168052275">Standing by the 5 stars. As I've said before, these people are too intimately wound up with my psyche to be rated objectively. <br/><br/>There's some preaching but to my eye it's not as heavy-handed as in Little Women. There are lots of great female role-models (with respect to the times). All of the young women are working toward careers, with the exception of Daisy (that natural housewife!). The young men are supportive and for the most part, respectful. There are anachronisms aplenty, but there's also </span>
  <span id="freeText11054976143168052275" style="display:none">Standing by the 5 stars. As I've said before, these people are too intimately wound up with my psyche to be rated objectively. <br /><br />There's some preaching but to my eye it's not as heavy-handed as in Little Women. There are lots of great female role-models (with respect to the times). All of the young women are working toward careers, with the exception of Daisy (that natural housewife!). The young men are supportive and for the most part, respectful. There are anachronisms aplenty, but there's also love and joy in abundance.<br /><br />If you haven't read the book and plan to, please stop reading now.<br />Spoilers below.<br /><br /><br />Kathleen asked, in the context of another review, if I thought that Dan was dismissed as a contender for Bess' affections because of his race. I said no at the time, and I still say no. Dan killed a man and served a prison term because of it, and that is the reason that there will be no "nice" woman for him. I still think that had he not done so, he'd have been unacceptable for Bess the mealy-mouthed perfect princess- for class reasons. His rough and tumble upbringing would be against him, in the eyes of the hyper-refined Mrs. Amy. Nat, who came from similar cellars, was much more malleable and weak. He became adequately civilized- but still wouldn't have been okay for Bess. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11054976143168052275" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_6717933" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/6717933" />
    <a title="The Library Lady" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/288297-the-library-lady"><img alt="The Library Lady" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1188780964p2/288297.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/6717933?book_show_action=true">Sep 24, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="The Library Lady" class="user" itemprop="url" name="The Library Lady" href="/user/show/288297-the-library-lady">The Library Lady</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/288297-the-library-lady?shelf=classics">classics</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer6717933" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10967816820052780241">This opens ten years after Little Men, though some of the youngest characters' ages seem a few years off! Alcott continues her alternative life for her stand in character, giving Jo her own literary success, including a funny chapter (which is clearly autobiographical) about being a celebrity in the late 19th century! But she also gives Jo the happy marriage and family she herself did not achieve. By now her sister May was gone, and her stand in Amy only gets a few lines, but it is noted that La</span>
  <span id="freeText10967816820052780241" style="display:none">This opens ten years after Little Men, though some of the youngest characters' ages seem a few years off! Alcott continues her alternative life for her stand in character, giving Jo her own literary success, including a funny chapter (which is clearly autobiographical) about being a celebrity in the late 19th century! But she also gives Jo the happy marriage and family she herself did not achieve. By now her sister May was gone, and her stand in Amy only gets a few lines, but it is noted that Laurie and Amy's marriage is a very happy one-- take that Team JoLaurie! Meg is present, but she is a boring pious widow except when she appears in the college play. There is fun with the young people of Plumfield as college students, who of course learn valuable life lessons from the wise March sisters, and Alcott, as she says, does not end with a grand catastrophe to firmly finish things off, but instead writes a paragraph or two giving everything she can a happy ending.<br /><br /> A lot of readers were probably disappointed in this book, but I think that knowing what lay behind it in the author's life gives the whole thing of great deal of poignancy.This last book in the series was written near the very end of Alcott's life, and it has a feel of final things.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10967816820052780241" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3059192249" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3059192249" />
    <a title="Elisa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/63369210-elisa"><img alt="Elisa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1581755382p2/63369210.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3059192249?book_show_action=true">Feb 27, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elisa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elisa" href="/user/show/63369210-elisa">Elisa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781540740212" href="/book/show/44667483-jo-s-boys">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3059192249" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17968975286901668513">I just finished JO'S BOYS by Louisa May Alcott and I have to admit, I was a little disappointed. It was wonderful to get a last glimpse into the March's family's life, but I enjoyed this book the least of all. For one, this book was very chaotic, which is why I didn't understand some chapters. Also, this book seemed to miss an overarching plot, resulting in a disconnection between chapters, which made reading this book not as enjoyable as the previous books. Moreover, the number of morals in thi</span>
  <span id="freeText17968975286901668513" style="display:none">I just finished JO'S BOYS by Louisa May Alcott and I have to admit, I was a little disappointed. It was wonderful to get a last glimpse into the March's family's life, but I enjoyed this book the least of all. For one, this book was very chaotic, which is why I didn't understand some chapters. Also, this book seemed to miss an overarching plot, resulting in a disconnection between chapters, which made reading this book not as enjoyable as the previous books. Moreover, the number of morals in this book seemed multiplied by 1000 compared to the previous books, and sometimes it was just a little too much. In her previous books on the March family, Alcott was able to create a perfect balance between adventure, fun, and morals, but in this book, the balance was way off. I also didn't agree with the ending, because it was extremely rushed and all. but one character had a happy ending, which didn't seem logical and Dan definitely deserved better, since he had already learned his lesson multiple times over. I had a hard time reading this book and didn't really enjoy myself, so, unfortunately, I am rating it with only ⭐⭐</span>
  <a data-text-id="17968975286901668513" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1605607839" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1605607839" />
    <a title="Michaila " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30216107-michaila"><img alt="Michaila " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1556031765p2/30216107.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1605607839?book_show_action=true">Apr 09, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michaila " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michaila " href="/user/show/30216107-michaila">Michaila </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1605607839" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5314128332904661243">The last book in the March family chronicles.<br/><br/>First off, I noticed there seemed to be much more words of wisdom from Jo and Fritz in this one. The fact that poor Dan, after all his struggling, never was married but loved Bess all the while, was very heartbreaking because he was one of my favorites. My favorite couple was either the brave Emil and Mary (because they had been so through so much, and helped one another survive through it all) or Demi and Alice, because of his shyness and the beautif</span>
  <span id="freeText5314128332904661243" style="display:none">The last book in the March family chronicles.<br /><br />First off, I noticed there seemed to be much more words of wisdom from Jo and Fritz in this one. The fact that poor Dan, after all his struggling, never was married but loved Bess all the while, was very heartbreaking because he was one of my favorites. My favorite couple was either the brave Emil and Mary (because they had been so through so much, and helped one another survive through it all) or Demi and Alice, because of his shyness and the beautiful rose proposal. I wanted to know more of little Jo; all we know is she was married well, and that her acting turned out wonderfully. <br /><br />Yet, overall, this book came quite close to bringing me to tears, and the wise, foolish, old and young characters were all vividly depicted as people in real life, just as Louisa May Alcott's books are. Full of real life lessons.<br /><br />5 stars!<br /><br />~Mic</span>
  <a data-text-id="5314128332904661243" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('seImDyPP+NXIhTXQ+NYKa83fMkpY/hH3shGOIMIvVT9EkWwh9srMCX7KjRxN+txafDTADMpSRd76ONajmSct/Q==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6606966-louisa-may-alcott"><img alt="Louisa May Alcott: The Woman Behind Little Women" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1441295382l/6606966._SX98_.jpg" />

<script>
//<![CDATA[
      var newTip = new Tip($('bookCover_6606966'), "\n\n  <h2><a class=\"readable bookTitle\" href=\"https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6606966-louisa-may-alcott?from_choice=false&amp;from_home_module=false\">Louisa May Alcott: The Woman Behind Little Women<\/a><\/h2>\n\n      <div>\n        by <a class=\"authorName\" href=\"/author/show/2983142.Harriet_Reisen?a=9&amp;origin=related_works\">Harriet Reisen<\/a>\n      <\/div>\n\n          <div class=\"smallText uitext darkGreyText\">\n            <span class=\"minirating\"><span class=\"stars staticStars notranslate\"><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p6\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p0\"><\/span><\/span> 3.92 avg rating &mdash; 1,528 ratings<\/span>            &mdash; published 2009\n          <\/div>\n\n    <div class=\"addBookTipDescription\">\n      \n<span id=\"freeTextContainer12515323773311296737\">A vivid, energetic account of the life of Louisa May Alcott, whose work has delighted millions of readers\n\nLouisa May Alcott portrays a writer as worthy of interest in her own right as her most famous character, Jo March, and addresses all aspects of<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText12515323773311296737\" style=\"display:none\">A vivid, energetic account of the life of Louisa May Alcott, whose work has delighted millions of readers\n\nLouisa May Alcott portrays a writer as worthy of interest in her own right as her most famous character, Jo March, and addresses all aspects of Alcott’s life: the effect of her father’s self-indulgent utopian schemes; her family’s chronic economic difficulties and frequent uprootings; her experience as a nurse in the Civil War; the loss of her health and frequent recourse to opiates in search of relief from migraines, insomnia, and symptomatic pain. Stories and details culled from Alcott’s journals; her equally rich letters to family, friends, publishers, and admiring readers; and the correspondence, journals, and recollections of her family, friends, and famous contemporaries provide the basis for this lively account of the author’s classic rags-to-riches tale.\n\nAlcott would become the equivalent of a multimillionaire in her lifetime based on the astounding sales of her books, leaving contemporaries like Nathaniel Hawthorne, Herman Melville, and Henry James in the dust. This biography explores Alcott’s life in the context of her works, all of which are to some extent autobiographical. A fresh, modern take on this remarkable and prolific writer, who secretly authored pulp fiction, harbored radical abolitionist views, and completed heroic service as a Civil War nurse, Louisa May Alcott is in the end also the story of how the all-time beloved American classic Little Women came to be.       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/1315.Louisa_May_Alcott">About Louisa May Alcott</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/1315.Louisa_May_Alcott"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1200326665p3/1315.jpg);'></div>

<a href="/author/show/1315.Louisa_May_Alcott">Louisa May Alcott

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer6366293877431520869">As <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2765771._A_M__Barnard' title=' A.M. Barnard' rel='nofollow noopener'> A.M. Barnard</a>: <br/>Behind a Mask, or a Woman's Power (1866)<br/>The Abbot's Ghost, or Maurice Treherne's Temptation (1867)<br/>A Long Fatal Love Chase (1866 – first published 1995)<br/>First published anonymously:<br/>A Modern Mephistopheles (1877)<br/><br/>Louisa May Alcott was born in Germantown, Pennsylvania on November 29, 1832. She and her three sisters, Anna, Elizabeth and May were educated by their father, philosopher/ t</span>
  <span id="freeText6366293877431520869" style="display:none">As <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2765771._A_M__Barnard" title=" A.M. Barnard" rel="nofollow noopener"> A.M. Barnard</a>: <br />Behind a Mask, or a Woman's Power (1866)<br />The Abbot's Ghost, or Maurice Treherne's Temptation (1867)<br />A Long Fatal Love Chase (1866 – first published 1995)<br />First published anonymously:<br />A Modern Mephistopheles (1877)<br /><br />Louisa May Alcott was born in Germantown, Pennsylvania on November 29, 1832. She and her three sisters, Anna, Elizabeth and May were educated by their father, philosopher/ teacher, Bronson Alcott and raised on the practical Christianity of their mother, Abigail May.<br /><br />Louisa spent her childhood in Boston and in Concord, Massachusetts, where her days were enlightened by visits to Ralph Waldo Emerson’s library, excursions into nature with Henry David Thoreau and theatricals in the barn at Hillside (now Hawthorne’s "Wayside").<br /><br />Like her character, Jo March in Little Women, young Louisa was a tomboy: "No boy could be my friend till I had beaten him in a race," she claimed, " and no girl if she refused to climb trees, leap fences...."<br /><br />For Louisa, writing was an early passion. She had a rich imagination and often her stories became melodramas that she and her sisters would act out for friends. Louisa preferred to play the "lurid" parts in these plays, "the villains, ghosts, bandits, and disdainful queens."<br /><br />At age 15, troubled by the poverty that plagued her family, she vowed: "I will do something by and by. Don’t care what, teach, sew, act, write, anything to help the family; and I’ll be rich and famous and happy before I die, see if I won’t!"<br /><br />Confronting a society that offered little opportunity to women seeking employment, Louisa determined "...I will make a battering-ram of my head and make my way through this rough and tumble world." Whether as a teacher, seamstress, governess, or household servant, for many years Louisa did any work she could find.<br /><br />Louisa’s career as an author began with poetry and short stories that appeared in popular magazines. In 1854, when she was 22, her first book Flower Fables was published. A milestone along her literary path was Hospital Sketches (1863) based on the letters she had written home from her post as a nurse in Washington, DC as a nurse during the Civil War.<br /><br />When Louisa was 35 years old, her publisher Thomas Niles in Boston asked her to write "a book for girls." Little Women was written at Orchard House from May to July 1868. The novel is based on Louisa and her sisters’ coming of age and is set in Civil War New England. Jo March was the first American juvenile heroine to act from her own individuality; a living, breathing person rather than the idealized stereotype then prevalent in children’s fiction.<br /><br />In all, Louisa published over 30 books and collections of stories. She died on March 6, 1888, only two days after her father, and is buried in Sleepy Hollow Cemetery in Concord.</span>
